<a href="/wiki/Lists_of_United_States_state_symbols" title="Lists of United States state symbols">Lists of United States state symbols</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Wyoming</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ŋ/: 'ng' in 'sing'">ŋ</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Wyoming.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e9/En-us-Wyoming.ogg" title="En-us-Wyoming.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>) is a state in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountain_States" title="Mountain States">mountain region</a> of the western <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The state is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">10th largest by area</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">least populous</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states by population density">second most sparsely populated state</a> in the country. Wyoming is bordered on the north by <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>, on the east by <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a>, on the south by <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, on the southwest by <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, and on the west by <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">Idaho</a> and Montana. The state population was estimated at 586,107 in 2015, which is less than 31 of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">most populous U.S. cities</a> including neighboring <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne,_Wyoming" title="Cheyenne, Wyoming">Cheyenne</a> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_capital" title="State capital">state capital</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Wyoming" title="List of municipalities in Wyoming">most populous city</a>, with population estimated at 63,335 in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cheyenne_Pop_Estimate_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cheyenne_Pop_Estimate-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>The western two-thirds of the state is covered mostly by the mountain ranges and rangelands of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>, while the eastern third of the state is high elevation prairie called the <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">High Plains</a>. Almost half of the land in Wyoming is owned by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">U.S. government</a>, leading Wyoming to rank sixth by area and fifth by proportion of a state's land owned by the federal government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maineenvironment.org_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-maineenvironment.org-9">[9]</a></sup> Federal lands include two national parks—<a href="/wiki/Grand_Teton_National_Park" title="Grand Teton National Park">Grand Teton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_National_Park" title="Yellowstone National Park">Yellowstone</a>—two national recreation areas, two national monuments, several national forests, historic sites, fish hatcheries, and wildlife refuges.
</p><p>Original inhabitants of the region include the <a href="/wiki/Crow_Nation" title="Crow Nation">Crow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arapaho" title="Arapaho">Arapaho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakota_people" title="Lakota people">Lakota</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shoshone" title="Shoshone">Shoshone</a>. Southwestern Wyoming was in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> and then Mexican territory until it was ceded to the United States in 1848 at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a>. The region acquired the name <i>Wyoming</i> when a bill was introduced to the U.S. Congress in 1865 to provide a "temporary government for <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Territory" title="Wyoming Territory">the territory of Wyoming</a>". The name was used earlier for the <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Valley" title="Wyoming Valley">Wyoming Valley</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, and is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Munsee_language" title="Munsee language">Munsee</a> word <i><i lang="umu" title="Munsee language text">xwé:wamənk</i></i>, meaning "at the big river flat".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bright,_William_2004_pg._576_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bright,_William_2004_pg._576-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_of_Wyoming_–_Narrative_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_Wyoming_–_Narrative-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>The main drivers of Wyoming's economy are mineral extraction—mostly <a href="/wiki/Coal_mining" title="Coal mining">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trona" title="Trona">trona</a>—and <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>. Agricultural commodities include <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> (beef), <a href="/wiki/Hay" title="Hay">hay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_beet" title="Sugar beet">sugar beets</a>, grain (<a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>. The climate is <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental</a>, drier and windier than the rest of the U.S., with greater temperature extremes.
</p><p>Wyoming has been a politically conservative state since the 1950s, with the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> candidate winning every presidential election except <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Wyoming,_1964" title="United States presidential election in Wyoming, 1964">1964</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leip_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-leip-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_K%C3%B6ppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1305" data-file-width="1260" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Wyoming_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/220px-Wyoming_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Wyoming_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/330px-Wyoming_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Wyoming_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/440px-Wyoming_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate types</a> of Wyoming</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Wyoming" title="Climate change in Wyoming">Climate change in Wyoming</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="652" data-file-width="677" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Wyoming.JPG/220px-Wyoming.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Wyoming.JPG/330px-Wyoming.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Wyoming.JPG/440px-Wyoming.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wyoming state welcome sign on <a href="/wiki/Interstate_80" title="Interstate 80">Interstate 80</a> in <a href="/wiki/Uinta_County,_Wyoming" title="Uinta County, Wyoming">Uinta County</a> (at the <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> border)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Autumn_in_the_Bighorn_Mountains.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Autumn_in_the_Bighorn_Mountains.JPG/220px-Autumn_in_the_Bighorn_Mountains.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Autumn_in_the_Bighorn_Mountains.JPG/330px-Autumn_in_the_Bighorn_Mountains.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Autumn_in_the_Bighorn_Mountains.JPG/440px-Autumn_in_the_Bighorn_Mountains.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Autumn_in_the_Bighorn_Mountains.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Autumn in the Bighorn Mountains</div></div></div>
<p>Wyoming's climate is generally <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_steppe" title="Cold steppe"><i>BSk</i></a></i>), and is drier and windier in comparison to most of the United States with greater temperature extremes. Much of this is due to the topography of the state. Summers in Wyoming are warm with July high temperatures averaging between 85 and 95 °F (29 and 35 °C) in most of the state. With increasing elevation, however, this average drops rapidly with locations above 9,000 feet (2,700 m) averaging around 70 °F (21 °C). Summer nights throughout the state are characterized by a rapid cooldown with even the hottest locations averaging in the 50–60 °F (10–16 °C) range at night. In most of the state, most of the precipitation tends to fall in the late spring and early summer. Winters are cold, but are variable with periods of sometimes extreme cold interspersed between generally mild periods, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinook_winds" title="Chinook winds">Chinook winds</a> providing unusually warm temperatures in some locations. Wyoming is a dry state with much of the land receiving less than 10 inches (250 mm) of rainfall per year. Precipitation depends on elevation with lower areas in the <a href="/wiki/Bighorn_Basin" title="Bighorn Basin">Big Horn Basin</a> averaging 5–8 inches (130–200 mm) (making the area nearly a true <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>). The lower areas in the North and on the eastern plains typically average around 10–12 inches (250–300 mm), making the climate there <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-arid" title="Semi-arid">semi-arid</a>. Some mountain areas do receive a good amount of precipitation, 20 inches (510 mm) or more, much of it as snow, sometimes 200 inches (510 cm) or more annually. The state's highest recorded temperature is 114 °F (46 °C) at <a href="/wiki/Basin,_Wyoming" title="Basin, Wyoming">Basin</a> on July 12, 1900 and the lowest recorded temperature is −66 °F (−54 °C) at <a href="/wiki/Riverside,_Wyoming" title="Riverside, Wyoming">Riverside</a> on February 9, 1933.
</p><p>The number of <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">thunderstorm</a> days vary across the state with the southeastern plains of the state having the most days of thunderstorm activity. Thunderstorm activity in the state is highest during the late spring and early summer. The southeastern corner of the state is the most vulnerable part of the state to <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornado</a> activity. Moving away from that point and westwards, the incidence of tornadoes drops dramatically with the west part of the state showing little vulnerability. Tornadoes, where they occur, tend to be small and brief, unlike some of those that occur a little farther east.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location_and_size">Location and size</span></h3>
<p>As specified in the designating legislation for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Wyoming" title="Territory of Wyoming">Territory of Wyoming</a>, Wyoming's borders are lines of <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> <a href="/wiki/41st_parallel_north" title="41st parallel north">41°N</a> and <a href="/wiki/45th_parallel_north" title="45th parallel north">45°N</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a> 104°3'W and 111°3'W (27° W and 34° W of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Meridian" title="Washington Meridian">Washington Meridian</a>), making the shape of the state a latitude-longitude quadrangle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Wyoming is one of only three states (along with <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>) to have borders along only straight latitudinal and longitudinal lines, rather than being defined by natural landmarks. Due to surveying inaccuracies during the 19th century, Wyoming's legal border deviates from the true <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> and <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a> lines by up to half of a mile (0.8 km) in some spots, especially in the mountainous region along the <a href="/wiki/45th_parallel_north" title="45th parallel north">45th parallel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Wyoming is bordered on the north by <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>, on the east by <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a>, on the south by <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, on the southwest by <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, and on the west by <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">Idaho</a>. It is the tenth largest state in the United States in total area, containing 97,814 square miles (253,340 km<sup>2</sup>) and is made up of 23 counties. From the north border to the south border it is 276 miles (444 km);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and from the east to the west border is 365 miles (587 km) at its south end and 342 miles (550 km) at the north end.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_landforms">Natural landforms</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mountain_ranges">Mountain ranges</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a> meet the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> in Wyoming. The state is a great <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateau</a> broken by many <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain ranges</a>. Surface elevations range from the summit of <a href="/wiki/Gannett_Peak" title="Gannett Peak">Gannett Peak</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Wind_River_Range" title="Wind River Range">Wind River Mountain Range</a>, at 13,804 feet (4,207 m), to the <a href="/wiki/Belle_Fourche_River" title="Belle Fourche River">Belle Fourche River</a> valley in the state's northeast corner, at 3,125 feet (952 m). In the northwest are the <a href="/wiki/Absaroka_Range" title="Absaroka Range">Absaroka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Owl_Creek_Mountains" title="Owl Creek Mountains">Owl Creek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gros_Ventre_Range" title="Gros Ventre Range">Gros Ventre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind_River_Range" title="Wind River Range">Wind River</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Teton_Range" title="Teton Range">Teton</a> ranges. In the north central are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Horn_Mountains" title="Big Horn Mountains">Big Horn Mountains</a>; in the northeast, the <a href="/wiki/Black_Hills" title="Black Hills">Black Hills</a>; and in the southern region the <a href="/wiki/Laramie_Mountains" title="Laramie Mountains">Laramie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicine_Bow_Mountains" title="Medicine Bow Mountains">Snowy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_Range_(Wyoming)" title="Sierra Madre Range (Wyoming)">Sierra Madre</a> ranges.
</p><p>The Snowy Range in the south central part of the state is an extension of the Colorado <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rockies</a> in both geology and appearance. The Wind River Range in the west central part of the state is remote and includes more than 40 mountain peaks in excess of 13,000 ft (4,000 m) tall in addition to Gannett Peak, the highest peak in the state. The Big Horn Mountains in the north central portion are somewhat isolated from the bulk of the Rocky Mountains.
</p><p>The Teton Range in the northwest extends for 50 miles (80 km), part of which is included in <a href="/wiki/Grand_Teton_National_Park" title="Grand Teton National Park">Grand Teton National Park</a>. The park includes the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Teton" title="Grand Teton">Grand Teton</a>, the second highest peak in the state.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_Divide" title="Continental Divide">Continental Divide</a> spans north-south across the central portion of the state. Rivers east of the divide drain into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Missouri_River_Basin" title="Missouri River Basin">Missouri River Basin</a> and eventually the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>. They are the <a href="/wiki/North_Platte_River" title="North Platte River">North Platte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind_River_(Wyoming)" title="Wind River (Wyoming)">Wind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bighorn_River" title="Bighorn River">Big Horn</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_River" title="Yellowstone River">Yellowstone</a> rivers. The <a href="/wiki/Snake_River" title="Snake River">Snake River</a> in northwest Wyoming eventually drains into the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_River" title="Columbia River">Columbia River</a> and the Pacific Ocean, as does the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_River_(Colorado_River)" title="Green River (Colorado River)">Green River</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado River</a> Basin.
</p><p>The Continental Divide forks in the south central part of the state in an area known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Divide_Basin" title="Great Divide Basin">Great Divide Basin</a> where the waters that flow or precipitate into this area remain there and cannot flow to any ocean. Instead, because of the overall aridity of Wyoming, water in the Great Divide Basin simply sinks into the soil or evaporates.
</p><p>Several rivers begin in or flow through the state, including the Yellowstone River, Bighorn River, Green River, and the Snake River.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands">Islands</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Wyoming" title="List of islands of Wyoming">List of islands of Wyoming</a></div>
<p>Wyoming has 32 named islands, the majority of which are located in <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Lake" title="Jackson Lake">Jackson Lake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_Lake" title="Yellowstone Lake">Yellowstone Lake</a> within <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_National_Park" title="Yellowstone National Park">Yellowstone National Park</a> in the northwest portion of the state. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_River_(Colorado_River)" title="Green River (Colorado River)">Green River</a> in the southwest also contains a number of islands.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions_and_administrative_divisions">Regions and administrative divisions</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Counties">Counties</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Wyoming" title="List of counties in Wyoming">List of counties in Wyoming</a></div>
<p>The state of Wyoming has 23 <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a>.
</p>

<p>In 2005, 50.6% of Wyomingites lived in one of the 13 most populous Wyoming municipalities.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_areas">Metropolitan areas</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> has defined two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_metropolitan_area" title="United States metropolitan area">Metropolitan Statistical Areas</a> (MSA) and seven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_micropolitan_area" title="United States micropolitan area">Micropolitan Statistical Areas</a> (MiSA) for the State of Wyoming. In 2008, 30.4% of Wyomingites lived in either of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_metropolitan_area" title="United States metropolitan area">Metropolitan Statistical Areas</a>, and 73% lived in either a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_metropolitan_area" title="United States metropolitan area">Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> or a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_micropolitan_area" title="United States micropolitan area">Micropolitan Statistical Area</a>.
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wind_River_Indian_Reservation">Wind River Indian Reservation</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wind_River_Indian_Reservation" title="Wind River Indian Reservation">Wind River Indian Reservation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WindRiverCanyon.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/WindRiverCanyon.JPG/220px-WindRiverCanyon.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/WindRiverCanyon.JPG/330px-WindRiverCanyon.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/WindRiverCanyon.JPG/440px-WindRiverCanyon.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WindRiverCanyon.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wind_River_Canyon" title="Wind River Canyon">Wind River Canyon</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Wind River <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Reservation" title="Indian Reservation">Indian Reservation</a> is shared by the <a href="/wiki/Shoshone" title="Shoshone">Eastern Shoshone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arapaho" title="Arapaho">Northern Arapaho</a> tribes of Native Americans in the central western portion of the state near <a href="/wiki/Lander,_Wyoming" title="Lander, Wyoming">Lander</a>. The reservation is home to 2,500 Eastern Shoshone and 5,000 Northern Arapaho.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Washakie" title="Chief Washakie">Chief Washakie</a> established the reservation in 1868<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shoshone_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-shoshone-24">[24]</a></sup> as the result of negotiations with the federal government in the <a href="/wiki/Fort_Bridger" title="Fort Bridger">Fort Bridger</a> Treaty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbs_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-pbs-25">[25]</a></sup> However, the Northern Arapaho were forced onto the Shoshone reservation in 1876 by the federal government after the government failed to provide a promised separate reservation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbs_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-pbs-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>Today the Wind River Indian Reservation is jointly owned, with each tribe having a 50% interest in the land, water, and other natural resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arapaho_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-arapaho-26">[26]</a></sup> The reservation is a sovereign, self-governed land with two independent governing bodies: the Eastern Shoshone Tribe and the Northern Arapaho Tribe. Until 2014, the Shoshone Business Council and Northern Arapaho Business Council met jointly as the Joint Business Council to decide matters that affect both tribes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shoshone_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-shoshone-24">[24]</a></sup> Six elected council members from each tribe served on the joint council.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_lands">Public lands</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_ref_2001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="590" data-file-width="757" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Wyoming_ref_2001.jpg/220px-Wyoming_ref_2001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Wyoming_ref_2001.jpg/330px-Wyoming_ref_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Wyoming_ref_2001.jpg/440px-Wyoming_ref_2001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_ref_2001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wyoming terrain map</div></div></div>
<p>More than 48% of the land in Wyoming is owned by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">U.S. government</a>, leading Wyoming to rank sixth in the United States in total acres and fifth in percentage of a state's land owned by the federal government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maineenvironment.org_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-maineenvironment.org-9">[9]</a></sup> This amounts to about 30,099,430 acres (121,808.1 km<sup>2</sup>) owned and managed by the United States government. The state government owns an additional 6% of all Wyoming lands, or another 3,864,800 acres (15,640 km<sup>2</sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maineenvironment.org_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-maineenvironment.org-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>The vast majority of this government land is administered by the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Land_Management" title="Bureau of Land Management">Bureau of Land Management</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Forest_Service" title="United States Forest Service">U.S. Forest Service</a> in numerous <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Forest" title="United States National Forest">national forests</a>, a <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Grassland" title="United States National Grassland">national grassland</a>, and a number of vast swathes of public land, in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Francis_E._Warren_Air_Force_Base" title="Francis E. Warren Air Force Base">Francis E. Warren Air Force Base</a> in Cheyenne.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_Wyoming_NPS_sites_USA.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="500" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Map_Wyoming_NPS_sites_USA.gif/220px-Map_Wyoming_NPS_sites_USA.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Map_Wyoming_NPS_sites_USA.gif/330px-Map_Wyoming_NPS_sites_USA.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Map_Wyoming_NPS_sites_USA.gif/440px-Map_Wyoming_NPS_sites_USA.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_Wyoming_NPS_sites_USA.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>National Park Service sites map</div></div></div>
<p>In addition, Wyoming contains areas managed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> and other agencies such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" title="United States Fish and Wildlife Service">U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service</a>, including:
</p><p><b>National parks</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Grand_Teton_National_Park" title="Grand Teton National Park">Grand Teton National Park</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_National_Park" title="Yellowstone National Park">Yellowstone National Park</a> – first designated national park in the world<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPindex_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-NPindex-27">[27]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p><b>Memorial parkway</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller_Jr._Memorial_Parkway" title="John D. Rockefeller Jr. Memorial Parkway">John D. Rockefeller Jr. Memorial Parkway</a> between Yellowstone and Grand Teton National Parks</li></ul>
<p><b>National recreation areas</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bighorn_Canyon_National_Recreation_Area" title="Bighorn Canyon National Recreation Area">Bighorn Canyon National Recreation Area</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flaming_Gorge_National_Recreation_Area" title="Flaming Gorge National Recreation Area">Flaming Gorge National Recreation Area</a> (managed by the Forest Service as part of <a href="/wiki/Ashley_National_Forest" title="Ashley National Forest">Ashley National Forest</a>)</li></ul>
<p><b>National monuments</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Devils_Tower" title="Devils Tower">Devils Tower National Monument</a> – first national monument in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPindex_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-NPindex-27">[27]</a></sup></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Wyoming" title="History of Wyoming">History of Wyoming</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Fort_Laramie_-_Walters_37194049.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1309" data-file-width="1800" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Fort_Laramie_-_Walters_37194049.jpg/220px-Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Fort_Laramie_-_Walters_37194049.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Fort_Laramie_-_Walters_37194049.jpg/330px-Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Fort_Laramie_-_Walters_37194049.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Fort_Laramie_-_Walters_37194049.jpg/440px-Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Fort_Laramie_-_Walters_37194049.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Fort_Laramie_-_Walters_37194049.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Laramie" title="Fort Laramie">Fort Laramie</a> as it looked before 1840 (painting from memory by Alfred Jacob Miller)</div></div></div>
<p>Several Native American groups originally inhabited the region now known as Wyoming. The <a href="/wiki/Crow_Nation" title="Crow Nation">Crow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arapaho" title="Arapaho">Arapaho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakota_people" title="Lakota people">Lakota</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shoshone" title="Shoshone">Shoshone</a> were but a few of the original inhabitants encountered when <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white</a> explorers first entered the region. What is now southwestern Wyoming became a part of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> and later Mexican territory of <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a>, until it was ceded to the United States in 1848 at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a>. French-Canadian trappers from Québec and Montréal went into the state in the late 18th century, leaving French toponyms such as Téton and <a href="/wiki/Jacques_La_Ramee" title="Jacques La Ramee">La Ramie</a>. <a href="/wiki/John_Colter" title="John Colter">John Colter</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Clark_Expedition" title="Lewis and Clark Expedition">Lewis and Clark Expedition</a>, itself guided by French Canadian <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Charbonneau" title="Toussaint Charbonneau">Toussaint Charbonneau</a> and his young Shoshone wife, <a href="/wiki/Sacagawea" title="Sacagawea">Sacagawea</a>, first described the region in 1807. At the time, his reports of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Yellowstone_Ecosystem" title="Greater Yellowstone Ecosystem">Yellowstone</a> area were considered to be fictional.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stuart_(explorer)" title="Robert Stuart (explorer)">Robert Stuart</a> and a party of five men returning from <a href="/wiki/Astoria,_Oregon" title="Astoria, Oregon">Astoria</a> discovered <a href="/wiki/South_Pass_(Wyoming)" title="South Pass (Wyoming)">South Pass</a> in 1812. The <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Trail" title="Oregon Trail">Oregon Trail</a> later followed that route. In 1850, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Bridger" title="Jim Bridger">Jim Bridger</a> located what is now known as <a href="/wiki/Bridger_Pass" title="Bridger Pass">Bridger Pass</a>, which the <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific Railroad</a> used in 1868—as did <a href="/wiki/Interstate_80_in_Wyoming" title="Interstate 80 in Wyoming">Interstate 80</a>, 90 years later. Bridger also explored Yellowstone and filed reports on the region that, like those of Colter, were largely regarded as <a href="/wiki/Tall_tale" title="Tall tale">tall tales</a> at the time.
</p><p>The region had acquired the name <i>Wyoming</i> by 1865, when Representative <a href="/wiki/James_Mitchell_Ashley" title="James Mitchell Ashley">James Mitchell Ashley</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> introduced a bill to Congress to provide a "temporary government for <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Territory" title="Wyoming Territory">the territory of Wyoming</a>". The territory was named after the <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Valley" title="Wyoming Valley">Wyoming Valley</a> in Pennsylvania, made famous by the 1809 poem <i><a href="/wiki/Gertrude_of_Wyoming" title="Gertrude of Wyoming">Gertrude of Wyoming</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Campbell_(poet)" title="Thomas Campbell (poet)">Thomas Campbell</a>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wyoming" title="Battle of Wyoming">Battle of Wyoming</a> in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>. The name ultimately derives from the <a href="/wiki/Munsee_language" title="Munsee language">Munsee</a> word <i><i lang="umu" title="Munsee language text">xwé:wamənk</i></i>, meaning "at the big river flat".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bright,_William_2004_pg._576_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bright,_William_2004_pg._576-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_of_Wyoming_–_Narrative_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_Wyoming_–_Narrative-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_Jeep_Trail.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1759" data-file-width="1164" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Wyoming_Jeep_Trail.JPG/170px-Wyoming_Jeep_Trail.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Wyoming_Jeep_Trail.JPG/255px-Wyoming_Jeep_Trail.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Wyoming_Jeep_Trail.JPG/340px-Wyoming_Jeep_Trail.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_Jeep_Trail.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A backcounty road in the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_Range_(Wyoming)" title="Sierra Madre Range (Wyoming)">Sierra Madre Range</a> of southeastern Wyoming near Bridger Peak</div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific Railroad</a> had reached the town of <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne,_Wyoming" title="Cheyenne, Wyoming">Cheyenne</a> in 1867, the region's population began to grow steadily, and the federal government established the Wyoming Territory on July 25, 1868.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Unlike mineral-rich <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, Wyoming lacked significant deposits of gold and silver, as well as Colorado's subsequent population boom. However, <a href="/wiki/South_Pass_City,_Wyoming" title="South Pass City, Wyoming">South Pass City</a> did experience a short-lived boom after the Carissa Mine began producing gold in 1867.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Furthermore, copper was mined in some areas between the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_Range_(Wyoming)" title="Sierra Madre Range (Wyoming)">Sierra Madre Mountains</a> and the Snowy Range near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Encampment,_Wyoming" title="Grand Encampment, Wyoming">Grand Encampment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>Once government-sponsored expeditions to the Yellowstone country began, reports by Colter and Bridger, previously believed to be apocryphal, were found to be true. This led to the creation of <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_National_Park" title="Yellowstone National Park">Yellowstone National Park</a>, which became the world's first <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national park</a> in 1872. Nearly all of Yellowstone National Park lies within the far northwestern borders of Wyoming.
</p><p>On December 10, 1869, territorial Governor <a href="/wiki/John_Allen_Campbell" title="John Allen Campbell">John Allen Campbell</a> extended the right to vote to women, making Wyoming the first territory and then United States state to grant <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> to women. In addition, Wyoming was also a pioneer in welcoming women into politics. Women first served on juries in Wyoming (<a href="/wiki/Laramie,_Wyoming" title="Laramie, Wyoming">Laramie</a> in 1870); Wyoming had the first female court bailiff (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mary_Atkinson_(bailiff)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mary Atkinson (bailiff) (page does not exist)">Mary Atkinson</a>, Laramie, in 1870); and the first female <a href="/wiki/Justice_of_the_peace" title="Justice of the peace">justice of the peace</a> in the country (<a href="/wiki/Esther_Hobart_Morris" title="Esther Hobart Morris">Esther Hobart Morris</a>, South Pass City, in 1870). Also, in 1924, Wyoming became the first state to elect a female governor, <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Tayloe_Ross" title="Nellie Tayloe Ross">Nellie Tayloe Ross</a>, who took office in January 1925.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Due to its civil-rights history, one of Wyoming's state nicknames is "The Equality State", and the official state motto is "Equal Rights".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WyoFacts_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-WyoFacts-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Wyoming's constitution included <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage" title="Women's suffrage">women's suffrage</a> and a pioneering article on <a href="/wiki/Water_right" title="Water right">water rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Congress admitted Wyoming into the Union as the 44th state on July 10, 1890.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WyoFacts_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-WyoFacts-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Wyoming was the location of the <a href="/wiki/Johnson_County_War" title="Johnson County War">Johnson County War</a> of 1892, which erupted between competing groups of cattle ranchers. The passage of the federal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homestead_Act" title="Homestead Act">Homestead Act</a> led to an influx of small ranchers. A <a href="/wiki/Range_war" title="Range war">range war</a> broke out when either or both of the groups chose violent conflict over commercial competition in the use of the public land.
</p>

text-align: center;">0.7%</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/1980_United_States_Census" title="1980 United States Census">1980</a></b></td><td style="padding-left:8px;">469,557</td><td style="font-size:85%"></td><td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">41.3%</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/1990_United_States_Census" title="1990 United States Census">1990</a></b></td><td style="padding-left:8px;">453,588</td><td style="font-size:85%"></td><td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">−3.4%</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/2000_United_States_Census" title="2000 United States Census">2000</a></b></td><td style="padding-left:8px;">493,782</td><td style="font-size:85%"></td><td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">14.1%</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b>Est. 2017</b></td><td style="padding-left:8px;">579,315</td><td style="font-size:85%"></td><td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">2.8%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; </tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_population_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="700" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Wyoming_population_map.png/300px-Wyoming_population_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Wyoming_population_map.png/450px-Wyoming_population_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Wyoming_population_map.png/600px-Wyoming_population_map.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_population_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wyoming population density map – the largest population centers are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheyenne,_WY_MSA" title="Cheyenne, WY MSA">Cheyenne</a> in the southeast and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Casper,_WY,_MSA" title="Casper, WY, MSA">Casper</a> in the east central section.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of Wyoming was 579,315 in 2017,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEst2017_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopEst2017-36">[36]</a></sup> which is an increase of 2.8% since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-7">[7]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> of Wyoming is located in <a href="/wiki/Natrona_County,_Wyoming" title="Natrona County, Wyoming">Natrona County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, the United States Census Bureau estimated that the racial composition of the population was 92.7% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">white</a> (82.9 non-Hispanic white), 2.7% American Indian and Alaska Native, 1.6% Black or African American, 1.0% Asian American, and 0.1% Native Hawaiian or Pacific Islander.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCB2012est_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-USCB2012est-39">[39]</a></sup> As of 2011, 24.9% of Wyoming's population younger than age 1 were minorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the 2010 census, the racial composition of the population was 90.7% white, 0.8% black or African American, 2.4% American Indian and Alaska Native, 0.8% Asian American, 0.1% Native Hawaiian and other Pacific Islander, 2.2% from two or more races, and 3.0% from some other race. Ethnically, 8.9% of the total population was of <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic</a> or Latino origin (they may be of any race) and 91.1% Non-Hispanic, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_white" title="Non-Hispanic white">non-Hispanic whites</a> constituting the largest non-Hispanic group at 85.9%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2015, Wyoming had an estimated population of 586,107, which was an increase of 1,954, or 0.29%, from the prior year and an increase of 22,481, or 3.99%, since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>. This includes a natural increase since the last census of 12,165 people (that is 33,704 births minus 21,539 deaths) and an increase from net migration of 4,035 people into the state. Immigration resulted in a net increase of 2,264 people, and migration within the country produced a net increase of 1,771 people. In 2004, the foreign-born population was 11,000 (2.2%). In 2005, total births in Wyoming numbered 7,231 (birth rate of 14.04 per thousand).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Sparsely populated, Wyoming is the least populous state of the United States. Wyoming has the second-lowest population density, behind <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>. It is one of only two states with a smaller population than the nation's capital, Washington, D.C. (the other state is <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>).
</p><p>According to the 2000 census, the largest ancestry groups in Wyoming are: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German-American" title="German-American">German</a> (26.0%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a> (16.0%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a> (13.3%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian-American" title="Norwegian-American">Norwegian</a> (4.3%), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish-American" title="Swedish-American">Swedish</a> (3.5%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_State_Capitol.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1680" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Wyoming_State_Capitol.jpg/220px-Wyoming_State_Capitol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Wyoming_State_Capitol.jpg/330px-Wyoming_State_Capitol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Wyoming_State_Capitol.jpg/440px-Wyoming_State_Capitol.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_State_Capitol.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wyoming State Capitol building, Cheyenne</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_government">State government</span></h3>
<p>Wyoming's Constitution established three branches of government: the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Wyoming" title="List of Governors of Wyoming">executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Legislature" title="Wyoming Legislature">legislative</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Supreme_Court" title="Wyoming Supreme Court">judicial</a> branches.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wyoming_State_Legislature" title="Wyoming State Legislature">Wyoming State Legislature</a> comprises a <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_House_of_Representatives" title="Wyoming House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a> with 60 members and a <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Senate" title="Wyoming Senate">Senate</a> with 30 members.
</p><p>The executive branch is headed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Wyoming" title="Governor of Wyoming">governor</a> and includes a <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_of_Wyoming" title="Secretary of State of Wyoming">secretary of state</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_State_Auditor" title="Wyoming State Auditor">auditor</a>, treasurer and superintendent of public instruction. Wyoming does not have a <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_governor_(United_States)#Wyoming" title="Lieutenant governor (United States)">lieutenant governor</a>. Instead the secretary of state stands first in the line of succession.
</p><p>Wyoming's sparse population warrants it only a single <a href="/wiki/At-large" title="At-large">at-large</a> seat in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</a>, and hence only three votes in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">Electoral College</a>.
</p><p>Wyoming is an <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage_control_state" title="Alcoholic beverage control state">alcoholic beverage control state</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_system">Judicial system</span></h3>
<p>Wyoming's highest court is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Wyoming" title="Supreme Court of Wyoming">Supreme Court of Wyoming</a>, with five justices presiding over appeals from the state's lower courts. Wyoming is unusual in that it does not have an intermediate <a href="/wiki/Appellate_court" title="Appellate court">appellate court</a>, like most states. This is largely attributable to the state's population and correspondingly lower caseload. Appeals from the state district courts go directly to the Wyoming Supreme Court. Wyoming also has state circuit courts (formerly county courts), of limited jurisdiction, which handle certain types of cases, such as civil claims with lower dollar amounts, misdemeanor criminal offenses, and <a href="/wiki/Felony" title="Felony">felony</a> <a href="/wiki/Arraignment" title="Arraignment">arraignments</a>. Circuit court judges also commonly hear small claims cases as well.
</p><p>Before 1972, Wyoming judges were selected by popular vote on a nonpartisan ballot. This earlier system was criticized by the state bar who called for the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Plan" title="Missouri Plan">Missouri Plan</a>, a system designed to balance judiciary independence with judiciary accountability. In 1972, an amendment to Article 5 of the Wyoming Constitution, which incorporated a modified version of the plan, was adopted by the voters. Since the adoption of the amendment, all state court judges in Wyoming are nominated by the Judicial Nominating Commission and appointed by the Governor. They are then subject to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Retention_vote" title="Retention vote">retention vote</a> by the electorate one year after appointment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p>

<p>Wyoming's political history defies easy classification. The state was the first to grant women the right to vote and to elect a woman governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Today_in_History_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Today_in_History-50">[50]</a></sup> On December 10, 1869, <a href="/wiki/John_Allen_Campbell" title="John Allen Campbell">John Allen Campbell</a>, the first Governor of the Wyoming Territory, approved the first law in United States history explicitly granting women the right to vote. This day was later commemorated as Wyoming Day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Today_in_History_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Today_in_History-50">[50]</a></sup> On November 5, 1889, voters approved the first constitution in the world granting full voting rights to women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memory.loc.gov_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-memory.loc.gov-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>While the state elected notable <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrats</a> to federal office in the 1960s and 1970s, politics have become decidedly more conservative since the 1980s as the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> came to dominate the state's congressional delegation. Today, Wyoming is represented in Washington by its two Senators, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Enzi" title="Mike Enzi">Mike Enzi</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Barrasso" title="John Barrasso">John Barrasso</a>, and its one member of the House of Representatives, Congresswoman <a href="/wiki/Liz_Cheney" title="Liz Cheney">Liz Cheney</a>. All three are Republicans. The state has not voted for a Democrat for president since 1964, one of only eight times since statehood. At present, there is only one relatively reliably Democratic county; affluent <a href="/wiki/Teton_County,_Wyoming" title="Teton County, Wyoming">Teton</a> and one swing county; college county <a href="/wiki/Albany_County,_Wyoming" title="Albany County, Wyoming">Albany</a>. In the 2004 presidential election, <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> won his second-largest victory, with 69% of the vote. Former Vice President <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cheney" title="Dick Cheney">Dick Cheney</a> is a Wyoming resident and represented the state in Congress from 1979 to 1989.
</p><p>Republicans are no less dominant at the state level. They have held a majority in the state senate continuously since 1936 and in the state house since 1964. However, Democrats held the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Wyoming" title="Governor of Wyoming">governorship</a> for all but eight years between 1975 and 2011. Uniquely, Wyoming elected Democrat <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Tayloe_Ross" title="Nellie Tayloe Ross">Nellie Tayloe Ross</a> as the first woman in United States history to serve as state governor. She served from 1925 to 1927, winning a special election after her husband, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Bradford_Ross" title="William Bradford Ross">William Bradford Ross</a>, unexpectedly died a little more than a year into his term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Wyoming" title="Political party strength in Wyoming">Political party strength in Wyoming</a></div>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Voter_registration_by_county">Voter registration by county</span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republicans</a> have a <a href="/wiki/Majority" title="Majority">majority</a> of registered votes in all but 2 counties: <a href="/wiki/Albany_County,_Wyoming" title="Albany County, Wyoming">Albany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teton_County,_Wyoming" title="Teton County, Wyoming">
Teton</a>, where they have a <a href="/wiki/Plurality_(voting)" title="Plurality (voting)">plurality</a> of registered voters.

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<p>In 2010, 93.39% (474,343) of Wyomingites over the age of 5 spoke <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> as their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_language" title="Primary language">primary language</a>. 4.47% (22,722) spoke <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, 0.35% (1,771) spoke <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, and 0.28% (1,434) spoke <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. Other common non-English languages included <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_languages" title="Algonquian languages">Algonquian</a> (0.18%), <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> (0.10%), <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> (both 0.09%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">American Community Survey</a> reported that 6.2% (30,419) of Wyoming's population over five years old spoke a language other than English at home. Of those, 68.1% were able to speak English very well, 16.0% spoke English well, 10.9% did not speak English well, and 5.0% did not speak English at all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Language2007_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Language2007-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<p>According to a 2013 Gallup Poll, the religious affiliations of the people of Wyoming were: 49% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">Protestants</a>, 18% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism_in_the_United_States" title="Catholicism in the United States">Catholics</a>, 9% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latter-day_Saint" title="Latter-day Saint">Latter-day Saints</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon" title="Mormon">Mormons</a>) and less than 1% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2010 ARDA report recognized as the largest denominations in Wyoming the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon" title="Mormon">Mormons</a>) with 62,804 (11%), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism_in_the_United_States" title="Catholicism in the United States">Catholic Church</a> with 61,222 (10.8%) and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a> with 15,812 adherents (2.8%). The same report counted 59,247 <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical Protestants</a> (10.5%), 36,539 <a href="/wiki/Mainline_Protestant" title="Mainline Protestant">Mainline Protestants</a> (6.5%), 785 <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Christians</a>; 281 <a href="/wiki/Black_church" title="Black church">Black Protestants</a>, as well as 65,000 adhering to other traditions and 340,552 not claiming any tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<p>Due to its sparse population, the state of Wyoming lacks any major professional sports teams. Some of the most popular sports teams in the state are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wyoming" title="University of Wyoming">University of Wyoming</a> <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Cowboys_and_Cowgirls" title="Wyoming Cowboys and Cowgirls">Cowboys and Cowgirls</a> teams – particularly football and basketball, which play in the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_West_Conference" title="Mountain West Conference">Mountain West Conference</a>. Their stadiums in Laramie are at about 7,200 feet (2,200 m) above sea level, the highest in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">NCAA Division I</a>. High school sports are governed by the <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_High_School_Activities_Association" title="Wyoming High School Activities Association">Wyoming High School Activities Association</a>, which sponsors 12 sports.
</p><p>Rodeo is popular in Wyoming, and Casper has hosted the <a href="/wiki/College_National_Finals_Rodeo" title="College National Finals Rodeo">College National Finals Rodeo</a> since 2001.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_symbols">State symbols</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indian_Paintbrush_in_Grand_Teton_NP-NPS.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1166" data-file-width="1517" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Indian_Paintbrush_in_Grand_Teton_NP-NPS.jpg/220px-Indian_Paintbrush_in_Grand_Teton_NP-NPS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Indian_Paintbrush_in_Grand_Teton_NP-NPS.jpg/330px-Indian_Paintbrush_in_Grand_Teton_NP-NPS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Indian_Paintbrush_in_Grand_Teton_NP-NPS.jpg/440px-Indian_Paintbrush_in_Grand_Teton_NP-NPS.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indian_Paintbrush_in_Grand_Teton_NP-NPS.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>State flower of Wyoming: Indian paintbrush</div></div></div>
