<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_infrastructure">Economy and infrastructure</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wyoming_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Wyoming locations by per capita income">Wyoming locations by per capita income</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wind_Power_4892597382.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Wind_Power_4892597382.jpg/220px-Wind_Power_4892597382.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Wind_Power_4892597382.jpg/330px-Wind_Power_4892597382.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Wind_Power_4892597382.jpg/440px-Wind_Power_4892597382.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wind_Power_4892597382.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">Wind farm</a> in <a href="/wiki/Uinta_County,_Wyoming" title="Uinta County, Wyoming">Uinta County</a></div></div></div>
<p>According to the 2012 United States Bureau of Economic Analysis report, Wyoming's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_state_product" title="Gross state product">gross state product</a> was $38.4 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> As of 2014 the population was growing slightly with the most growth in tourist-oriented areas such as <a href="/wiki/Teton_County,_Wyoming" title="Teton County, Wyoming">Teton County</a>. Boom conditions in neighboring states such as <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a> were drawing energy workers away. About half of Wyoming's counties showed population losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CST032915_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-CST032915-60">[60]</a></sup> The state makes active efforts through Wyoming Grown, an internet-based recruitment program, to find jobs for young people educated in Wyoming who have emigrated but may wish to return.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT71515_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT71515-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of November 2015, the state's unemployment rate was 4.0%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
The composition of Wyoming's economy differs significantly from that of other states with most activity in tourism, agriculture, and energy extraction; and little in anything else.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT71515_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT71515-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>The mineral extraction industry and travel and tourism sector are the main drivers behind Wyoming's economy. The federal government owns about 50% of its landmass, while 6% is controlled by the state. Total taxable values of mining production in Wyoming for 2001 was over $6.7 billion. The <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism industry</a> accounts for over $2 billion in revenue for the state.
</p><p>In 2002, more than six million people visited Wyoming's <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a> and monuments. The key tourist attractions in Wyoming include <a href="/wiki/Grand_Teton_National_Park" title="Grand Teton National Park">Grand Teton National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_National_Park" title="Yellowstone National Park">Yellowstone National Park</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Devils_Tower_National_Monument" title="Devils Tower National Monument">Devils Tower National Monument</a>, <a href="/wiki/Independence_Rock_(Wyoming)" title="Independence Rock (Wyoming)">Independence Rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fossil_Butte_National_Monument" title="Fossil Butte National Monument">Fossil Butte National Monument</a>. Each year Yellowstone National Park, the world's first national park, receives three million visitors.
</p><p>Historically, agriculture has been an important component of Wyoming's economy. Its overall importance to the performance of Wyoming's economy has waned. However, agriculture is still an essential part of Wyoming's culture and lifestyle. The main agricultural commodities produced in Wyoming include livestock (beef), <a href="/wiki/Hay" title="Hay">hay</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_beets" title="Sugar beets">sugar beets</a>, grain (wheat and barley), and <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>. More than 91% of land in Wyoming is classified as rural.
</p><p>Wyoming is the home of only a handful of companies with a regional or national presence.  <a href="/wiki/Taco_John%27s" title="Taco John's">Taco John's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Trading_Post" title="Sierra Trading Post">Sierra Trading Post</a>, both in Cheyenne, are privately held.  <a href="/wiki/Cloud_Peak_Energy" title="Cloud Peak Energy">Cloud Peak Energy</a> in Gillette and U.S. Energy Corp. (NASDAQ: USEG) in Riverton are Wyoming's only publicly traded companies. 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mineral_and_energy_production">Mineral and energy production</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Liebherr_T282C_Coal_Haul_Truck.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Liebherr_T282C_Coal_Haul_Truck.png/220px-Liebherr_T282C_Coal_Haul_Truck.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Liebherr_T282C_Coal_Haul_Truck.png/330px-Liebherr_T282C_Coal_Haul_Truck.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Liebherr_T282C_Coal_Haul_Truck.png/440px-Liebherr_T282C_Coal_Haul_Truck.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Liebherr_T282C_Coal_Haul_Truck.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A P&amp;H 4100 shovel loads coal into a Liebherr T 282C haul truck at the <a href="/wiki/North_Antelope_Rochelle_Mine" title="North Antelope Rochelle Mine">North Antelope Rochelle Mine</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Wyoming's mineral commodities include coal, natural gas, <a href="/wiki/Coalbed_methane" title="Coalbed methane">coalbed methane</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trona" title="Trona">trona</a>.
</p>
<ul><li>Coal: Wyoming produced 395.5 million short tons (358.8 million metric tons) of coal in 2004, greater than any other state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Wyoming possesses a reserve of 68.7 billion tons (62.3 billion metric tons) of coal. Major coal areas include the <a href="/wiki/Powder_River_Basin" title="Powder River Basin">Powder River Basin</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_River_Basin" title="Green River Basin">Green River Basin</a></li>
<li>Coalbed methane (CBM): The boom for CBM began in the mid-1990s. CBM is characterized as methane gas that is extracted from Wyoming's coal bed seams. It is another means of natural gas production. There has been substantial CBM production in the <a href="/wiki/Powder_River_Basin" title="Powder River Basin">Powder River Basin</a>. In 2002, the CBM production yield was 327.5 billion cubic feet (9.3 km<sup>3</sup>).</li>
<li>Crude oil: Wyoming produced 53.4 million barrels (8.49<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup> m<sup>3</sup>) of crude oil in 2007. The state ranked fifth nationwide in oil production in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-petro_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-petro-64">[64]</a></sup> Petroleum is most often used as a motor fuel, but it is also utilized in the manufacture of plastics, paints, and synthetic rubber.</li>
<li>Diamonds: The <a href="/wiki/Kelsey_Lake_Diamond_Mine" title="Kelsey Lake Diamond Mine">Kelsey Lake Diamond Mine</a>, located in Colorado less than 1,000 feet (300 m) from the Wyoming border, produced gem quality diamonds for several years. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wyoming_craton" title="Wyoming craton">Wyoming craton</a>, which hosts the <a href="/wiki/Kimberlite" title="Kimberlite">kimberlite</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_pipe" title="Volcanic pipe">volcanic pipes</a> that were mined, underlies most of Wyoming.</li>
<li>Natural gas: Wyoming produced 1.77 trillion cubic feet (50.0 billion m<sup>3</sup>) of natural gas in 2016. The state ranked 6th nationwide for natural gas production in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The major markets for natural gas include industrial, commercial, and domestic heating.</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rig_wind_river.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="835" data-file-width="741" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Rig_wind_river.jpg/220px-Rig_wind_river.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Rig_wind_river.jpg/330px-Rig_wind_river.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Rig_wind_river.jpg/440px-Rig_wind_river.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rig_wind_river.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Drilling_rig" title="Drilling rig">drilling rig</a> drills for natural gas just west of the <a href="/wiki/Wind_River_Range" title="Wind River Range">Wind River Range</a> in the Wyoming <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rockies</a>.</div></div></div>
<ul><li>Trona: Wyoming possesses the world's largest known reserve of <a href="/wiki/Trona" title="Trona">trona</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gearino_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-gearino-66">[66]</a></sup> a mineral used for manufacturing glass, paper, soaps, baking soda, water softeners, and pharmaceuticals. In 2008, Wyoming produced 46 million short tons (41.7 million metric tons) of trona, 25% of the world's production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gearino_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-gearino-66">[66]</a></sup></li>
<li>Wind power: Because of Wyoming's geography and high-altitude, the potential for <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Wyoming" title="Wind power in Wyoming">wind power in Wyoming</a> is one of the highest of any state in the US. The <a href="/wiki/Chokecherry_and_Sierra_Madre_Wind_Energy_Project" title="Chokecherry and Sierra Madre Wind Energy Project">Chokecherry and Sierra Madre Wind Energy Project</a> is the largest commercial wind generation facility under development in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carbon_County,_Wyoming" title="Carbon County, Wyoming">Carbon County</a> is home to the largest proposed wind farm in the US. However, construction plans have been halted because of proposed new taxes on wind power energy production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li>Uranium: Although <a href="/wiki/Uranium_mining_in_Wyoming" title="Uranium mining in Wyoming">uranium mining in Wyoming</a> is much less active than it was in previous decades, recent increases in the price of <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> have generated new interest in uranium prospecting and mining.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxes">Taxes</span></h3>
<p>Unlike most other states, Wyoming does not levy an individual or corporate <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>. In addition, Wyoming does not assess any tax on retirement income earned and received from another state. Wyoming has a state <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> of 4%. Counties have the option of collecting an additional 1% tax for general revenue and a 1% tax for specific purposes, if approved by voters. Food for human consumption is not subject to sales tax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> There also is a county lodging tax that varies from 2% to 5%. The state collects a <a href="/wiki/Use_tax" title="Use tax">use tax</a> of 5% on items purchased elsewhere and brought into Wyoming.
All <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">property tax</a> is based on the assessed value of the property and Wyoming's Department of Revenue's Ad Valorem Tax Division supports, trains, and guides local government agencies in the uniform assessment, valuation and taxation of locally assessed property. "Assessed value" means taxable value; "taxable value" means a percent of the fair market value of property in a particular class. Statutes limit property tax increases. For county revenue, the property tax rate cannot exceed 12 <a href="/wiki/Mill_(currency)" title="Mill (currency)">mills</a> (or 1.2%) of assessed value. For cities and towns, the rate is limited to 8 <a href="/wiki/Mill_(currency)" title="Mill (currency)">mills</a> (0.8%). With very few exceptions, state law limits the property tax rate for all governmental purposes.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Personal_property" title="Personal property">Personal property</a> held for personal use is tax-exempt. Inventory if held for resale, pollution control equipment, cash, accounts receivable, stocks and bonds are also exempt. Other exemptions include property used for religious, educational, charitable, fraternal, benevolent and government purposes and improvements for handicapped access. Mine lands, underground mining equipment, and oil and gas extraction equipment are exempt from property tax but companies must pay a gross products tax on minerals and a <a href="/wiki/Severance_tax" title="Severance tax">severance tax</a> on mineral production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>Wyoming does not collect <a href="/wiki/Inheritance_tax" title="Inheritance tax">inheritance taxes</a>. There is limited <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Estate_tax" title="Estate tax">estate tax</a> related to federal estate tax collection.
</p><p>In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Tax_Foundation" title="Tax Foundation">Tax Foundation</a> ranked Wyoming as having the single most "business friendly" tax climate of all 50 states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Wyoming state and local governments in fiscal year 2007 collected $2.242 billion in taxes, levies, and royalties from the oil and gas industry. The state's mineral industry, including oil, gas, <a href="/wiki/Trona" title="Trona">trona</a>, and coal provided $1.3 billion in property taxes from 2006 mineral production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-petro_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-petro-64">[64]</a></sup> Wyoming receives more federal tax dollars per capita in aid than any other state except Alaska. The federal aid per capita in Wyoming is more than double the United States average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2016, Wyoming does not require the beneficial owners of LLCs to be disclosed in the filing, which creates an opportunity for a tax haven, according to <a href="/wiki/Clark_Stith" title="Clark Stith">Clark Stith</a> of Clark Stith &amp; Associates in Rock Springs, Wyoming, a former Republican candidate for Wyoming secretary of state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PANAMA_PAPERS_INCLUDE_NEVADA,_WYOMING_AMONG_OFFSHORE_TAX_HAVENS_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-PANAMA_PAPERS_INCLUDE_NEVADA,_WYOMING_AMONG_OFFSHORE_TAX_HAVENS-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National-atlas-wyoming.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="576" data-file-width="755" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/National-atlas-wyoming.PNG/300px-National-atlas-wyoming.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/National-atlas-wyoming.PNG/450px-National-atlas-wyoming.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/National-atlas-wyoming.PNG/600px-National-atlas-wyoming.PNG 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National-atlas-wyoming.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Wyoming - <a class="external text" href="http://nationalatlas.gov/printable/images/pdf/reference/pagegen_wy.pdf" rel="nofollow">PDF</a></div></div></div>
<p>The largest airport in Wyoming is <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Hole_Airport" title="Jackson Hole Airport">Jackson Hole Airport</a>, with over 500 employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Three interstate highways and thirteen United States highways pass through Wyoming. In addition, the state is served by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_highways_in_Wyoming" title="State highways in Wyoming">Wyoming state highway system</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Interstate_25_in_Wyoming" title="Interstate 25 in Wyoming">Interstate 25</a> enters the state south of Cheyenne and runs north, intersecting Interstate 80 immediately west of Cheyenne. It passes through <a href="/wiki/Casper,_Wyoming" title="Casper, Wyoming">Casper</a> and ends at Interstate 90 near <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_Wyoming" title="Buffalo, Wyoming">Buffalo</a>. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_80_in_Wyoming" title="Interstate 80 in Wyoming">Interstate 80</a> crosses the Utah border west of <a href="/wiki/Evanston,_Wyoming" title="Evanston, Wyoming">Evanston</a> and runs east through the southern third of the state, passing through Cheyenne before entering Nebraska near <a href="/wiki/Pine_Bluffs,_Wyoming" title="Pine Bluffs, Wyoming">Pine Bluffs</a>. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_90_in_Wyoming" title="Interstate 90 in Wyoming">Interstate 90</a> comes into Wyoming near <a href="/wiki/Parkman,_Wyoming" title="Parkman, Wyoming">Parkman</a> and cuts through the northeastern part of the state. It serves <a href="/wiki/Gillette,_Wyoming" title="Gillette, Wyoming">Gillette</a> and enters South Dakota east of <a href="/wiki/Sundance,_Wyoming" title="Sundance, Wyoming">Sundance</a>.
</p><p>U.S. Routes <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_14" title="U.S. Route 14">14</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_16" title="U.S. Route 16">16</a>, and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_20#Eastern_Section" title="U.S. Route 20">the eastern section of U.S. 20</a> all have their western terminus at the eastern entrance to Yellowstone National Park and pass through <a href="/wiki/Cody,_Wyoming" title="Cody, Wyoming">Cody</a>. U.S. 14 travels eastward before joining I-90 at <a href="/wiki/Gillette,_Wyoming" title="Gillette, Wyoming">Gillette</a>. U.S. 14 then follows I-90 to the South Dakota border. U.S. 16 and 20 split off of U.S. 14 at <a href="/wiki/Greybull,_Wyoming" title="Greybull, Wyoming">Greybull</a> and U.S. 16 turns east at <a href="/wiki/Worland,_Wyoming" title="Worland, Wyoming">Worland</a> while U.S. 20 continues south <a href="/wiki/Shoshoni,_Wyoming" title="Shoshoni, Wyoming">Shoshoni</a>. <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_287" title="U.S. Route 287">U.S. Route 287</a> carries traffic from <a href="/wiki/Fort_Collins,_Colorado" title="Fort Collins, Colorado">Fort Collins, Colorado</a> into <a href="/wiki/Laramie,_Wyoming" title="Laramie, Wyoming">Laramie, Wyoming</a> through a pass between the <a href="/wiki/Laramie_Mountains" title="Laramie Mountains">Laramie Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Medicine_Bow_Mountains" title="Medicine Bow Mountains">Medicine Bow Mountains</a>, merges with US 30 and I-80 until it reaches Rawlins, where it continues north, passing Lander. Outside of <a href="/wiki/Moran,_Wyoming" title="Moran, Wyoming">Moran</a>, U.S. 287 is part of a large interchange with U.S. Highways 26, 191, and 89, before continuing north to the southern entrance of Yellowstone. U.S. 287 continues north of Yellowstone, but the two sections are separated by the national park.
</p><p>Other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Numbered_Highways" title="United States Numbered Highways">U.S. highways</a> that pass through the state are United States Highways are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_18_(Wyoming)" title="U.S. Highway 18 (Wyoming)">18</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_26_(Wyoming)" title="U.S. Highway 26 (Wyoming)">26</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_30_(Wyoming)" title="U.S. Highway 30 (Wyoming)">30</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_85_(Wyoming)" title="U.S. Highway 85 (Wyoming)">85</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_87_(Wyoming)" title="U.S. Highway 87 (Wyoming)">87</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_89_(Wyoming)" title="U.S. Highway 89 (Wyoming)">89</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_189_(Wyoming)" title="U.S. Highway 189 (Wyoming)">189</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_191_(Wyoming)" title="U.S. Highway 191 (Wyoming)">191</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_212_(Wyoming)" title="U.S. Highway 212 (Wyoming)">212</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_287_(Wyoming)" title="U.S. Highway 287 (Wyoming)">287</a>.
</p><p>Wyoming is one of only two states (the other being <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a>) in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/48_contiguous_states" title="48 contiguous states">48 contiguous states</a> not served by <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Wyoming_railroads" title="List of Wyoming railroads">List of Wyoming railroads</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Wyoming" title="List of airports in Wyoming">List of airports in Wyoming</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_highways_in_Wyoming" title="State highways in Wyoming">State highways in Wyoming</a></div>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rocky_Mountain_Herbarium_University_of_Wyoming.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Rocky_Mountain_Herbarium_University_of_Wyoming.JPG/220px-Rocky_Mountain_Herbarium_University_of_Wyoming.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Rocky_Mountain_Herbarium_University_of_Wyoming.JPG/330px-Rocky_Mountain_Herbarium_University_of_Wyoming.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Rocky_Mountain_Herbarium_University_of_Wyoming.JPG/440px-Rocky_Mountain_Herbarium_University_of_Wyoming.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rocky_Mountain_Herbarium_University_of_Wyoming.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Rocky Mountain Herbarium at the University of Wyoming</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_Wyoming" title="List of high schools in Wyoming">List of high schools in Wyoming</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_education" title="Public education">Public education</a> is directed by the state superintendent of public instruction, an elected state official. Educational policies are set by the State Board of Education, a nine-member board appointed by the governor. The constitution prohibits the state from establishing curriculum and textbook selections; these are the prerogatives of local school boards. The <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_School_for_the_Deaf" title="Wyoming School for the Deaf">Wyoming School for the Deaf</a> was the only in-state school dedicated to supporting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deaf" title="Deaf">deaf</a> students in Wyoming, but it closed in the summer of 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Wyoming" title="List of colleges and universities in Wyoming">List of colleges and universities in Wyoming</a></div>
<p>Wyoming has one public four-year institution, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wyoming" title="University of Wyoming">University of Wyoming</a> in <a href="/wiki/Laramie,_Wyoming" title="Laramie, Wyoming">Laramie</a> and one private four-year college, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Catholic_College" title="Wyoming Catholic College">Wyoming Catholic College</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Lander,_Wyoming" title="Lander, Wyoming">Lander</a>, Wyoming. In addition, there are seven two-year <a href="/wiki/Community_college" title="Community college">community colleges</a> spread throughout the state.
</p><p>Before the passing of a new law in 2006, Wyoming had hosted unaccredited institutions, many of them suspected <a href="/wiki/Diploma_mill" title="Diploma mill">diploma mills</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The 2006 law is forcing unaccredited institutions to make one of three choices: move out of Wyoming, close down, or apply for accreditation. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oregon_State_Office_of_Degree_Authorization" title="Oregon State Office of Degree Authorization">Oregon State Office of Degree Authorization</a> predicts that in a few years the problem of diploma mills in Wyoming might be resolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
